Using Water with Invisible Impurity and Ghusala
Ruling with evidence using consensus and taharrin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing wudu from water containing invisible impurity or ghusala, and apply the principle of taharrin when impurity is suspected.

Core Idea
If impurity is invisible, water remains pure for wudu—consensus confirms this.

This lesson addresses two scenarios: water with visible impurity (requiring taharrin to determine safe distance) and water used for purification (ghusala) where impurity is invisible. The Hanafi school, citing consensus from al-Khulasa, permits wudu from the spot where ghusala fell, provided no visible change occurred. A minority disagreement from ad-Dhakhira is dismissed as invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses (1) moving away from visible impurity in a water source, and (2) performing wudu from the spot where ghusala (wash water) fell. Recognize each as a distinct scenario.
The first issue involves taharrin (estimation); the second is a consensus ruling.
2
Note the preferred method for visible impurity
For visible impurity in a large water source, one must make an estimation (taharrin) to determine if the impurity reached the spot. If it did not, wudu is permissible.
This is the view preferred by the author of al-Bahr and Sharh al-Munya.
3
Understand the consensus on ghusala
The text states 'this is a ruling by consensus' from al-Khulasa. Even if ghusala is considered impure by some, its impurity is invisible, so wudu from its spot is allowed.
Consensus (ijma) is a binding proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Recognize the basis: invisibility
The effective cause is that the impurity (if any) is not visible. Hanafi fiqh treats invisible impurity as negligible for the permissibility of water usage.
If the water changes visibly, it becomes impure regardless.
5
Evaluate the dismissed objection
The author notes that ad-Dhakhira records a disagreement, but asserts its invalidity. This shows the preferred view is settled and the objection is not accepted.
Tarjih (preference) has already been made by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل من الجانب الآخر. اختلف في مقدار التنحي على أقوال ذكرناها في «السعاية»، والذي صححه صاحب «البحر» تبعاً لشارح «المنية» أنه يتحرى ، فإن وقع تحريه على أنّ النجاسة لم تخلص إلى هذا الموضع جاز منه الوضوء.
[۲] قوله وكذا من موضع غسالته؛ هذا حكم إجماعي كما صرح به في «الخلاصة» ، فإنّه إن كان الماء المستعمل طاهراً فظاهر، ولأنه كان نجساً فكذلك؛ لكون نجاسته غير مرئية، وذكر في «الذخيرة» خلافاً فيه، وقد بينا بطلانه في «السعاية».
Rather, from the other side. There is difference of opinion on the amount of moving away, on which we have mentioned the statements in 'as-Sa'aya'. The one which the author of 'al-Bahr' corrected, following the commentator of 'al-Munya', is that he makes an estimation (taharrin). If his estimation leads to the conclusion that the impurity did not reach this spot, then wudu from it is permissible. [2] His statement: 'And similarly from the spot of its wash water (ghusala).' This is a ruling by consensus as explicitly stated in 'al-Khulasa'. For if the used water is pure, then it is apparent; and if it was impure, then similarly due to its impurity being invisible. It was mentioned in 'ad-Dhakhira' that there is a disagreement about it, and we have shown its invalidity in 'as-Sa'aya'.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence. The author addresses two issues: first, the distance one must move away from visible impurity in a large water source. The preferred view is that one should perform ijtihad (taharrin) to determine if the impurity has spread; if it hasn't, wudu is permissible. Second, the case where the impurity is invisible (such as used water that is considered impure by some). The author states it is a matter of consensus (ijma) that one may perform wudu even from the exact spot where the wash water fell, because its impurity is not visible. The reference to 'ad-Dhakhira' about disagreement is dismissed as invalid. This reflects the Hanafi position that invisibility of impurity allows use of the water.

Key Terms
غسالة (ghusala): The water that falls from a limb during ablution; considered used water (mā' musta'mal).
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid act of purification.
تحري (taharrin): The process of making a reasonable estimation (ijtihad) regarding the spread of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the consensus mentioned in 'al-Khulasa', is it permissible to perform wudu from the exact spot where ghusala (wash water) fell in a large basin?
A) No, because ghusala is impure.
B) Yes, because the impurity is invisible and there is consensus on permissibility.
C) Only if the water has been moved.
D) Only if the basin is larger than ten by ten cubits.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wudu from water containing invisible impurity or ghusala, relying on consensus that invisibility preserves purity.

Hanafi Critique of 'Ten by Ten' Estimation
Critique of the Hanafi estimation of water quantity for preventing impurity spread

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi estimation of ten-by-ten cubits for water purity, identify the Shafi'i and Maliki alternatives, and state the relied-upon Hanafi position based on change.

Core Idea
A valid legal estimation must have a scriptural basis or consensus; personal opinion alone is insufficient.

This lesson critiques a Hanafi estimation regarding water purity: the idea that a basin of ten by ten cubits prevents impurity from spreading. The author, citing al-Baghawi, argues that this estimation has no basis in revelation or consensus. We will compare it with the Shafi'i reliance on the hadith of two qullahs and the Maliki reliance on change in water properties. Understanding this critique clarifies the correct Hanafi position, which is actually based on taghayyur, not a fixed quantity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine what exactly is being disputed: the criterion for when water remains pure after contact with impurity. The Hanafi estimation of ten-by-ten is one proposed criterion.
The central issue is the legal basis for water purity standards.
2
Analyze the criticized Hanafi position
Examine the 'ten by ten' estimation: it is a scholarly opinion (ra'y) without explicit scriptural support. The author dismisses it as lacking a valid legal source (asl shar'i).
This estimation is not attributed to the founding Hanafi authorities; it is a later development.
3
Contrast with Shafi'i and Maliki proofs
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith of two qullahs (qullatayn), which provides a fixed quantity. The Maliki school uses the principle of change (taghayyur) in water properties. Both bases are considered more sound.
The hadith is authentic according to Shafi'is, though Hanafis debate its reliability.
4
Determine the actual Hanafi relied-upon view
The authoritative Hanafi position is not the ten-by-ten estimation, but rather the criterion of taghayyur: water is pure unless a change occurs in color, taste, or smell. This aligns with the Maliki view.
Thus the critique is of a non-standard opinion within the Hanafi school.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Shafi'i view, water less than two qullahs becomes impure upon contact with impurity even without change. Under the Hanafi (and Maliki) view, as long as no change occurs, the water remains pure, regardless of quantity.
This affects daily scenarios like falling into a small pond or large tank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السنة : التَّقدير بعشر في عشر لا يرجع إلى أصل شرعي يُعْتَمَدُ عليه. قوله : قال محيي السنّة؛ هو أبو محمد الحسين بن مسعود البغوي، مؤلف «شرح السنّة»، و«مصابيح السنّة» في الحديث، ومعالم التنزيل» في التفسير، وغيرها، وقد مرت ترجمته في المقدمة. [٢]قوله : إلى أصل شرعي يعتمد عليه؛ يريد أنّ التقدير لا مدخل فيه للرأي، بل لا بد أن يكون له أصل شرعي من الكتاب والسنّة صراحة أو استنباطاً، أو كان وقع عليه الإجماع، والتقدير الذي ذكره الحنفيّة في عدم سراية النجاسة – أي العشر في العشر - ليس له أصل شرعي، بخلاف تقدير الشافعية به بقلتين، فإنه ثابت بالحديث الصحيح، وكذا تقدير المالكية بالتغيّر.
The Sunnah: The estimation of ten by ten does not go back to a valid legal source that can be relied upon. His statement: 'Muhyi as-Sunnah said' - he is Abu Muhammad al-Husayn ibn Mas'ud al-Baghawi, author of 'Sharh as-Sunnah', 'Masabih as-Sunnah' in hadith, and 'Ma'alim at-Tanzil' in tafsir, and others. His biography has passed in the introduction. [2] His statement: 'to a valid legal source that can be relied upon' - he means that estimation has no room for personal opinion; rather it must have a legal source from the Book or Sunnah explicitly or by inference, or be subject to consensus. The estimation mentioned by the Hanafis regarding non-prevalence of impurity - i.e., ten by ten - has no legal source, unlike the estimation of the Shafi'is of two qullahs, for it is established by an authentic hadith, and likewise the estimation of the Malikis by change.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the standard for determining when water does not become impure by contact with impurity. The author cites al-Baghawi to criticize the Hanafi practice of estimating a basin of ten by ten cubits as sufficient to prevent impurity from spreading. This estimation, he argues, has no basis in revelation or consensus. In contrast, the Shafi'i school uses the measure of two qullahs (about 270 liters) which is supported by a hadith, and the Maliki school relies on change (taghayyur) in the water. The Hanafi position is thus criticized as relying on an arbitrary figure. This shows that the authoritative view for Hanafis is actually based on other principles (such as change), not on the ten-by-ten estimation, which some later scholars used.

Key Terms
قلتان (qullatayn): Two qullahs; a specific volume measure (about 270 liters) used by Shafi'is to determine if water is immune to impurity.
تغير (taghayyur): Change in one of the three properties (color, taste, smell) of water due to impurity.
عشر في عشر (ashr fi ashr): Ten by ten; a Hanafi estimation that a basin of 10x10 cubits prevents impurity spread.
أصل شرعي (asl shar'i): A valid legal source from the Qur'an, Sunnah, or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Shafi'i estimation of two qullahs regarding water purity?
A) Consensus of the Sahaba.
B) An authentic hadith.
C) A rational analogy (qiyas).
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon criterion for water purity is change (taghayyur), not a fixed quantity like ten-by-ten or two qullahs.

Deriving the 10×10 Pond Size from Well Precinct Hadith
Explaining the derivation of the 10×10 size for a large pond from the well precinct hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a 10×10 pond and explain how the well precinct hadith serves as its proof via istidlal.

Core Idea
A pond's purity on the opposite side from impurity is estimated by analogy to the well's harim: 10 cubits each way.

In Hanafi taharah, a large stagnant pond (ghadir) is treated differently from a small pool. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the classic 10×10 cubit measurement — a size that ensures impurity in one part does not affect the rest. We will trace the textual evidence (the hadith on well precincts) and the analogical extension (qiyas) that supports it, while acknowledging that this estimation is a later scholarly refinement, not the original ruling of Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
State the original ruling
The passage begins with the ruling that if impurity falls in one side of a large pond, wudu is permissible from the other side because the water does not move from one end to the other.
This ruling is based on the natural stillness of large ponds; it predates any fixed measurement.
2
Identify the later estimation
Later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirun) estimated this 'large pond' as having dimensions of 10 cubits by 10 cubits. This estimation was made for practical ease (tashil) and to give a concrete guideline.
The estimation is not from the Qur'an or a direct hadith; it is a juristic derivation.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'Whoever digs a well, around it are forty cubits' is cited. It establishes a precinct (harim) of 40 cubits around a well, i.e., 10 cubits from each side. This indicates that the influence of the well (water attraction) does not extend beyond 10 cubits.
The hadith is marfu' but has slight weakness; however, it is considered acceptable for this ruling.
4
Apply the analogy
By qiyas, the same limit of 10 cubits is applied to the pond: just as the well's harim prevents digging beyond 10 cubits, so does the pond's size prevent impurity from spreading beyond 10 cubits.
The analogy is based on the common illa (effective cause) of preventing harm (i.e., water contamination).
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi development
The passage notes that this estimation is not the original position of Abu Hanifa himself but a later refinement. Original riwayat did not specify a size. The later scholars (like the author of this commentary) rely on it for fatwa.
This shows that the Hanafi madhhab evolves through tarjih and tashil (easing).

أقول : أصل المسألة أنَّ الغدير العظيم الذي لا يتحرك أحد طرفيه بتحريكِ الطرف الآخر إذا وقعت النَّجاسة في أحد جوانبه جاز الوضوء في الجانب الآخر ، ثمَّ قُدرَ هذا بعشر في عشر ، وإنما قُدِّر به بناءً على قولهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «مَنْ حَفَرَ بِثْرَا فَدَ حَوْلَهَا أَرْبَعُون ذِرَاعاً»، فيكون له حريمها من كل جانب عشرة، ففهم من هذا أَنَّهُ ١ ] قوله : أصل المسألة ؛ لما كان التقديرُ بالعشر في العشر المذكور في المتون، وقد اشتهر أن المتون موضوعة لنقل المذهب ، فكان مظنَّة أن يتوهم أن هذا التقدير هو أصلُ مذهب أبي حنيفة الله ، وأن إيراد الشافعية واردّ عليه، أشار إلى دفعه بأنّ التقدير إنما صدر من المشايخ توضيحاً وتخريجاً وتسهيلاً، وأصلُ المذهب غيره، ولا يَرِدُ عليه ما السنة له ، فإن إيراده لو صح إنما يرد على ما اختاره من التقدير. وفيه أيضاً : إشارة إلى أنّ كون المتونِ موضوعة لنقل أصل المذهب حكم أكثري لا كلي، وإلى أنه لو لم يتحصل أصل لذلك التقدير لم يقدح في أصل المذهب. [٣] قوله : من حفر بئراً ... الخ ، هذا الحديث أخرجه أحمد من حديث أبي هريرة ، وابن ماجه والطبراني من حديث عبد الله بن المغفل له، وأبو يوسف في «كتاب الخراج» من حديث الحسن البصري الله مرسلا ، كلهم رووه مرفوعا إلى النبي ، وفي أسانيده ضعف . يسير، كما حققه الزيلعي في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية). (۱) من حديث أبي هريرة وعبد الله بن مغفل الله في سنن ابن ماجه (۲) : ۸۳۱)، و(مسند أحمد» (٢: ٤٩٤)، و(سنن الدارقطني (٤) : (۲۲۰)، والتحقيق في أحاديث الخلاف (٢ : ٢٢٥)، وقد استوفى طرقه الزيلعي في نصب الراية (٤) : ۲۹۱ - (۲۹۲)، ورد كلام الدارقطني بأن الصحيح أنه مرسل. إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر في حريمها بشراً يُمنع منه لأنه ينجذب الماء إليها، وينقص الماء في . البئر الأُولَى ، وإن أراد أن يحفر بئر بالوعة يُمْنَعُ أيضاً ؛ لسرايةِ النَّجاسةِ إلى البئرِ الأولى، وتنجيس مائها، ولا يُمْنَعُ منها فيما وراء الحريم، وهو عشر في عشر، فعُلِمَ أَنَّ الشَّرعَ اعتبر العشرة في العشرة في عدم سراية النجاسة ، حتى لو كانت النَّجاسة تسري ، يحكم بالمنع ، ثمَّ المتأخّرونَ وسُّعُوا الأمر على النَّاسِ، وجوزوا الوضوء في جميع جوانبه. الماء من البئر الأولى إلى الثانية، فلصاحب الأولى أن يمنعه من ذلك، ويهدم ما حفره الثاني، وكذلك لو شاء الثاني أن يبني في ذلك الموضع بناء أو يزرع فيه زرعاً ، كان للأول أن يمنع منه. كذا في «كتاب الخراج» للإمام أبي يوسف . [١]قوله : بئر بالوعة ؛ هي بئر تحفر ضيّقة الرأس لماء المطر وغيره ، يعني إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر حفرة لإلقاء البالوعة - وهي القذرة والنجاسات ونحوها - ، وسيلان الميزاب في حريم البئر الأولى لا يسعه ذلك. [٢] قوله : فعلِمَ ... الخ ؛ خلاصة الاستدلال أنه فهم من حديث الحريم أنّ حفر بئر الماء أو بئر النجاسة في مقدار عشرة أذرع من البئر الأولى لا يجوز، وليس ذلك إلا السراية الماء والنجاسة إلى هذا المقدار، فعُلِمَ منه أنَّ الشرعَ اعتبر العشر في سراية النجاسةِ وعدم سرايتها، فلذلك قدَّرَ الفقهاء الحوض بالعشر في العشر، وحكموا بأن في هذا المقدار لا تسري النجاسة من جانب إلى جانب. وهاهنا أبحاث من وجوه : الأول : ما نقله صاحب «البحر» عن يعقوب باشا أنّ قوام الأرضِ أضعاف قوام الماء، فقياسه عليها في مقدار عدم السراية غير مستقيم. الثاني : إن كون الحريم من كل جانب عشرة إنّما هو قول البعض، والأصح أن الحريم من كل جانب أربعون ، قال صاحب الهداية»(۳) : هو الصحيح ، واختاره
I say: The basis of the issue is that a great pond, one part of which does not move by moving the other part, if impurity falls in one of its sides, it is permissible to perform ablution on the other side. Then this was estimated as ten by ten. It was estimated based on his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever digs a well, around it are forty cubits.' So its precinct from each side is ten. So it is understood from this that... [Commentary]
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqaya regarding the ruling on a large pond of stagnant water. The author first states the original ruling: if impurity falls in one side of such a pond, the other side remains pure for wudu. Then he explains that the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) estimated this pond as being 10x10 cubits in size. He then provides the proof: the hadith of the Prophet (SAW) about digging a well and its precinct (harim) being 40 cubits total, i.e., 10 cubits from each side. The author clarifies that this hadith is used to establish the principle that impurity does not spread beyond 10 cubits. The commentary then addresses potential misunderstandings: first, that the estimation is not the original ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa but rather a later clarification; second, that the hadith has some weakness but is accepted in this context. It also discusses the application: if someone wants to dig a well or a cesspit within the precinct, the owner of the first well can prevent it because the water or impurity would travel that distance. Finally, the author notes that later scholars eased the matter and allowed wudu from all sides of the pond. The passage also mentions two research points: a critique by Ya'qub Pasha that the analogy between water and earth is not sound, and the disagreement about the precinct size being 10 cubits versus 40 cubits.

Key Terms
الغدير (al-ghadir): A large pond or pool of stagnant water.
الحريم (al-harim): The precinct or inviolable zone around a well or property.
الذراع (al-dhira'): Cubit, a unit of length approximately 18-24 inches.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that a pond estimated at 10x10 cubits allows wudu from the side opposite an impurity?
A) It is an arbitrary estimation by later scholars.
B) It is derived from the Quranic verse about purification.
C) It is analogically derived from the hadith about the precinct of a well.
D) It is based on consensus (ijma) of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for a large pond's purity relies on a well-established hadith about well precincts, demonstrating the school's use of qiyas and later scholarly refinement (tashil) to derive practical rulings.

The Hareem of a Well: 10 Cubits or 40? A Hanafi Internal Critique
Critique of the deduced 10-cubit hareem rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute over the hareem measure and explain why the 10-cubit rule is considered a facilitative inference, not a primary text.

Core Idea
The 10-cubit hareem is a juristic inference; the stronger view is 40 cubits, but the school's ruling on impurity does not depend on it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah critiques the standard Hanafi estimation of the protected zone (hareem) around a well as 10 cubits on each side. The commentator presents multiple objections from later scholars and concludes that the correct measure is 40 cubits, yet the 10-cubit rule remains a practical facilitation. Let us follow the analysis step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
This passage addresses the protection of wells from harm, whether by water loss or impurity transmission. The hareem is the zone within which digging is prohibited.
The core ruling is about preventing harm (darar).
2
State the rule as given in the matn
The base text states the hareem is ten by ten cubits, and any excavation within that is preventable by the well owner.
This is the standard position attributed to Abu Yusuf in Kitab al-Kharaj.
3
Follow the four objections (abhath)
The commentator lists four critiques: 1) earth density vs water density makes analogy weak; 2) the correct hareem is actually 40 cubits per al-Hidayah; 3) the hadith implies a larger basin; 4) the 10-cubit rule is inferential, not explicit, so it cannot specify general texts.
These objections show the depth of Hanafi internal critique.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The commentator concludes that despite the weakness of the 10-cubit inference, the school's core ruling on small water impurity is well-established by other hadiths; the estimation is merely for facilitation (tashil).
The principle 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' applies: the ruling stands on its own evidence.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The dispute about the hareem measure does not change the fundamental ruling that small water becomes impure. The fatwa may use either measure, but the precautionary view is 40 cubits.
The thamarah al-khilaf is in the scope of prohibited digging, not in the purity of water.

كتاب الطهارة/ أقسام المياه إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر في حريمها بشراً يُمنع منه لأنه ينجذب الماء إليها، وينقص الماء في البئر الأولى، وإن أراد أن يحفر بئر بالوعة يُمْنَعُ أيضاً ؛ لسرايةِ النَّجاسةِ إلى البئرِ الأولى، وتنجيس مائها، ولا يُمْنَعُ منها فيما وراء الحريم، وهو عشر في عشر، فعُلِمَ أَنَّ الشَّرعَ اعتبر العشرة في العشرة في عدم سراية النجاسة ، حتى لو كانت النَّجاسة تسري ، يحكم بالمنع ، ثمَّ المتأخّرونَ وسُّعُوا الأمر على النَّاسِ، وجوزوا الوضوء في جميع جوانبه. الماء من البئر الأولى إلى الثانية، فلصاحب الأولى أن يمنعه من ذلك، ويهدم ما حفره الثاني، وكذلك لو شاء الثاني أن يبني في ذلك الموضع بناء أو يزرع فيه زرعاً ، كان للأول أن يمنع منه. كذا في «كتاب الخراج» للإمام أبي يوسف .
[١]قوله : بئر بالوعة ؛ هي بئر تحفر ضيّقة الرأس لماء المطر وغيره ، يعني إذا أراد آخر أن يحفر حفرة لإلقاء البالوعة - وهي القذرة والنجاسات ونحوها - ، وسيلان الميزاب في حريم البئر الأولى لا يسعه ذلك.
[٢] قوله : فعلِمَ ... الخ ؛ خلاصة الاستدلال أنه فهم من حديث الحريم أنّ حفر بئر الماء أو بئر النجاسة في مقدار عشرة أذرع من البئر الأولى لا يجوز، وليس ذلك إلا السراية الماء والنجاسة إلى هذا المقدار، فعُلِمَ منه أنَّ الشرعَ اعتبر العشر في سراية النجاسةِ وعدم سرايتها، فلذلك قدَّرَ الفقهاء الحوض بالعشر في العشر، وحكموا بأن في هذا المقدار لا تسري النجاسة من جانب إلى جانب.
وهاهنا أبحاث من وجوه :
الأول : ما نقله صاحب «البحر» عن يعقوب باشا أنّ قوام الأرضِ أضعاف قوام الماء، فقياسه عليها في مقدار عدم السراية غير مستقيم.
الثاني : إن كون الحريم من كل جانب عشرة إنّما هو قول البعض، والأصح أن الحريم من كل جانب أربعون ، قال صاحب الهداية»(۳) : هو الصحيح ، واختاره المصنف والشارح في «كتاب إحياء الموات»، وعليه حملوا حديث الحريم، يعني أنّ معناه أربعون من كل جانب، وإذا بطل الأصل بطل الفرع. البعض. فإن قلت : يكفي في بيان أصل العشر كون الحريم بقدر العشر من كل جانب عند قلت : فحينئذ يكون الأصل مرجوحاً ضعيفاً غير معتمد عليه، وهذا هو مفاد إيراد الشافعية.
الثالث : إنَّ مقتضى حديث الحريم لو سُلّم ما ذكره أن يكون الحوض أكثر من عشر في عشر ليتصوّر بين النجاسة وبين محلّ الطهارة هذا القدر.
الرابع : إن هذا الأصل بعد تمامه إنّما هو استنباطي ليس بصريحي، فلا يصلح مخصصاً لعموم حديث : الماء طهور لا ينجسه شيء، إلا ما غير طعمه أو لونه أو ريحه)، وغير ذلك من الأخبار. وفي المقام أبحاث أخر أيضاً مبسوطة في «السعاية»، وبالجملة فما أبداه الشارح له من الأصل ليس بمعتمد عليه ، والحق أنّ عدم تأصل التقدير بالعشر لا يقدح في أصل المذهب () ، ولا حاجة إلى تأصيله على أصل معتمد عليه ، فإنّ هذا التقدير وأمثاله إنما هو للتسهيل.
(۲) (۱) سبق تخريجه ، فما ذكره الشارح له من الحديث وإن سلم أنه غير مخصص لهذا الحديث ، لكنه مخصص بأحاديث أخرى كثيرة منها كما قال القاري في «فتح باب العناية»(۱ : ۸۷) : أنه «ليس على إطلاقه لقوله : لا يَبُولَنَّ أحدكم في الماء الدائم ولا يَغْتَسِلَنَّ فيه من الجنابة»، أو : «ثُمَّ يغتسل منه أو : «فيه» كما هو رواية «الصحيحين». فلو لم يكن مُفْسِداً للماء لما كان للنهي عنه فائدة.
(٢) أقول ما أبداه اللكنوي من أن عدم التأصل للعشر لا يقدح في أصل المذهب، كلام لطيف وجيه، لكن تأصيل الشارح له له ، بديع، يدل على دقة فهمه، وعمق نظره ؛ إذ أن نجاسة الماء القليل ثابتة بكثير من الأدلة مثل : حديث لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء الراكد»، وحديث «إذا ولغ الكلب في إناء أحدكم»، وغيرها، فكان لا بد من حد فاصل للقليل والكثير، فاستئناس
Book of Purification / Categories of Water. If someone else wants to dig a well in its protected area (hareem), he is prevented because water is drawn to it, and the water in the first well decreases. And if he wants to dig a cesspool (bi'r baloo'ah), he is also prevented, due to the transmission of impurity (najasah) to the first well and the impurity of its water. But he is not prevented from doing so beyond the hareem, which is ten by ten (cubits). So it is known that the Law considered ten by ten (cubits) as preventing the transmission of impurity, such that if the impurity were to transmit, prohibition would be ruled. Then the later scholars made it easy for people and permitted ablution (wudu) from all its sides. The water from the first well to the second: the owner of the first may prevent him from that and demolish what the second dug. Likewise, if the second wishes to build a structure or plant a crop in that place, the first may prevent him. Thus in the Kitab al-Kharaj of Imam Abu Yusuf. [1] His statement: "cesspool well" is a well dug narrow at the top for rainwater and other things, meaning if someone else wants to dig a pit for throwing garbage—which is filth and impurities and the like—and the flow of the drainspout into the hareem of the first well, he is not allowed that. [2] His statement: "So it is known..." etc. The summary of the inference is that from the hadith of hareem, it is understood that digging a water well or a well of impurity within ten cubits of the first well is not permissible, and that is only due to the transmission of water and impurity to this extent. So it is known from this that the Law considered the ten (cubits) as a boundary for the transmission or non-transmission of impurity. Therefore, the jurists estimated the basin (hawd) as ten by ten and ruled that within this amount, impurity does not transmit from one side to the other. Here there are investigations from several aspects: First: What the author of al-Bahr reported from Ya'qub Pasha that the density of earth is many times that of water, so analogizing it to the measure of non-transmission is unsound. Second: That the hareem being ten from each side is only the saying of some; the more correct (asahh) is that the hareem is forty from each side, said the author of al-Hidayah: it is the correct view, and it was chosen by the author (al-Marghinani) and the commentator in the book Ihya' al-Mawat, and upon it they interpreted the hadith of hareem, meaning its meaning is forty from each side, and if the foundation is invalidated, the branch is invalidated. Some (say). If you say: It suffices for establishing the basis of ten that the hareem is ten from each side according to some. I say: Then the foundation would be weak, not relied upon, and this is the import of the Shafi'i objection. Third: That the implication of the hadith of hareem, even if what he mentioned is conceded, would be that the basin is more than ten by ten to conceive of this amount between the impurity and the place of purity. Fourth: That this foundation, even after its completion, is merely inferential (istinbati), not explicit (sarihi), so it is not suitable to specify (takhsis) the general meaning of the hadith: "Water is pure, nothing makes it impure except what changes its taste, color, or smell," and other reports. Other investigations are also detailed in al-Sa'ayah. In summary, what the commentator presented as a foundation is not reliable, and the truth is that the lack of a solid basis for the estimation of ten does not harm the principle of the school (asl al-madhhab), and there is no need to base it on a reliable foundation, for this estimation and its like are merely for facilitation. (2) (1) Its takhrij was given earlier. What the commentator presented from the hadith, even if it is conceded that it does not specify (takhsis) this hadith, it is specified by many other hadith, including as al-Qari said in Fath Bab al-Inayah (1:87): that "it is not absolute due to his saying: 'None of you should urinate in stagnant water nor bathe in it from janabah,' or 'then bathe from it' or 'in it' as in the narration of the Two Sahihs. If it were not spoiling the water, the prohibition would have no benefit." (2) I say: What al-Lakhnawi expressed—that the lack of a foundation for the ten does not harm the principle of the school—is a subtle and sound statement. But the commentator's founding of it is ingenious, indicating precision of understanding and depth of insight. Indeed, the impurity of small water is established by many proofs such as the hadith "None of you should urinate in still water" and the hadith "When a dog drinks from a vessel of one of you," etc. So there had to be a dividing limit between little and much; therefore, an inference was made.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the Hanafi ruling regarding the protected zone (hareem) around a well. The commentator (likely from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) starts by stating the standard Hanafi position: if someone digs a well or cesspool within the hareem (ten cubits on each side) of an existing well, the owner of the first well may prevent it because it either draws away water or transmits impurity. The hareem is defined as ten cubits on each side (عشر في عشر). The author explains that this measure is derived (فهم) from the hadith of hareem, which was interpreted to mean that within ten cubits impurity does not transmit. However, the commentator then presents four objections (أبحاث) from later scholars: 1) The density of earth vs. water makes analogy unsound; 2) The correct hareem is actually forty cubits (as per al-Hidayah and the preferred view); 3) If impurity does transmit, the basin would need to be larger than ten cubits; 4) The ten-cubit rule is an inference (استنباطي), not an explicit text, so it cannot specify the general hadith that water is pure unless changed. The commentator concludes that even though the specific estimation of ten cubits lacks a strong textual basis, this does not invalidate the fundamental Hanafi ruling (اصل المذهب) that small water becomes impure. The estimation is simply a facilitative tool. The final addition by al-Lakhnawi (and the commentator) defends the school by noting that the impurity of small water is well-established by other hadith, and a boundary between little and much water was needed, hence the jurists made this reasonable estimation.

Key Terms
حريم (hareem): The protected area around a well within which no excavation or construction may take place that would harm the well.
عشر في عشر (ashrun fi ashr): Ten cubits in each direction, i.e., a square area of 10x10 cubits around the well.
سراية النجاسة (sarayat al-najasah): The transmission or seepage of impurity (najasah) from one location to another, especially through water or moisture in the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view preferred in this passage, what is the correct measure of the hareem around a well?
A) 10 cubits from each side
B) 40 cubits from each side
C) 20 cubits from each side
D) 5 cubits from each side

Key Takeaway
The 10-cubit hareem is a facilitative estimation; the stronger view is 40 cubits, but both serve to protect wells from harm.

Key Terms and Conditions for Used Water (Ma' Musta'mal)
Commentary defining terms and conditions for invalidating used water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two causes that render water musta'mal, define qurbah/ta'ah/'ibadah, and apply the rule that musta'mal water is tahir but not mutahhir.

Core Idea
Used water loses purity capacity by devotion or impurity removal; intention doesn't matter.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary unpacks the concise matn 'Nor with water used for devotion or for removal of impurity.' The author clarifies the precise meanings of qurbah, ta'ah, and 'ibadah, and explains that water becomes musta'mal (used) in two distinct ways: when used for a devotional act (even without removing impurity) or when used to remove impurity (even without devotional intent). Understanding these categories is essential for correctly applying the ruling that musta'mal water is pure (tahir) but cannot purify (mutahhir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage comments on the statement 'Nor with water used for devotion or for removal of impurity.' The ruling is that such water cannot be used for purification (wudu, ghusl). Recognize that this is a general prohibition; the commentary explains its scope.
The matn is from al-Wiqayah, a core Hanafi text.
2
Define the three categories: qurbah, ta'ah, 'ibadah
The author distinguishes acts by whether they require intention and knowledge. Qurbah: reward after knowing the one you draw near, intention not required. Ta'ah: reward with or without intention, knowledge not required. 'Ibadah: reward requires intention. Note examples: prayers are all three; Quran recitation is qurbah and ta'ah but not 'ibadah.
These definitions affect which acts make water musta'mal.
3
Understand the first cause: use for devotion (qurbah)
If water is used with the goal of acquiring reward, even if no impurity is removed (e.g., wudu on wudu), it becomes musta'mal. 'Qurbah' here refers to the reward itself, not the act's name.
This covers voluntary ablutions.
4
Understand the second cause: use for impurity removal (raf' hadath)
If water is used to remove impurity, even without devotional intent (e.g., unintentional wudu), it becomes musta'mal. The 'lam' in 'li-raf' hadath' indicates consequence, not motive.
This rebuts the objection that removal always involves intention.
5
Apply the ruling and note the cross-madhhab difference
Hanafis hold musta'mal water is tahir but not mutahhir (cannot be used for fard purification). Shafi'is consider it purifying for non-obligatory acts. Understand the practical implication: a Hanafi cannot use leftover wudu water for another wudu.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بماء استعمل لقربة أو لرفع حدث
اعلم أن في الماء المستعمل اختلافات : قوله : ولا بماء ; أي لا يجوز الوضوء بماء مستعمل، وكذا الغُسل واستعماله الذي يخرجه عن طهوريته، يكون بأمرين : أحدهما : أن يستعمله لأجل قُربة - وهي بالضم – : عبارة عن فعل ما يثاب عليه بعد معرفة من يتقرب إليه، وإن لم يتوقف على نية. وأما الطاعة : فهي عبارة عن فعل ما يثاب عليه توقف على نية أم لا، عرف ما يفعله لأجله أم لا. والعبادة : ما يثاب على فعله، ويتوقف على نيّة، فالصلوات الخمس والصوم ونحوهما قُربات وعبادات وطاعات. وقراءة القرآن قُربة وطاعة لا عبادة. والنظر المؤدي إلى معرفة الله طاعة لا قربةٌ ولا عبادة. كذا في «حواشي الأشباه» للحموي. والمراد بالقربة هاهنا نفس الثواب إطلاقاً لاسم الفعل على أثره، فالحاصل أنّ الذي استعمل لغرض تحصيل الثواب أعم من أن يرتفع به الحدث : كالوضوء لرفع الحدث، أو لم يرتفع : كالوضوء على الوضوء لا يجوز به التطهير. وثانيهما : أن يستعمله بغرض رفع حدث، سواء كان لقربة أيضاً : كالوضوء المنوي أو كالوضوء الغير المنوي عندنا. وبهذا وضح لك أنّ النسبة بين الاستعمال للقربة وبين الاستعمال لرفع الحدث، نسبة العموم والخصوص من وجه ، وإن كلمة : «أو» في كلام المصنف لمنع الخلو; لعدم امتناع الجمع، وإن اللام الداخلة على القربة للغرض، لكن بمعنى العاقبة لا بما يكون مقصوداً من الفعل وباعثاً له، فاندفع ما أورد أنَّ الاستعمال لرفع الحدث لا ينفك عن النية، فلا يشمل رفعه بدون نيّة وأمّا حمل اللام على الوقت كما اختاره الناظرون الشارح له في تقدير ذلك في محله، ومن أراد الاستفاضة في أدلة ذلك فليراجع المطولات ولا يغتر بكلام المحشي هاهنا ، فإن أدلة الحنفية ظاهرة جلية في هذا المقام، والله أعلم.
Nor with water used for an act of devotion or for removal of impurity. Know that there are differences regarding used water: His statement: 'Nor with water' means it is not permissible to perform ablution with used water, and likewise for ritual bath. Its use that removes it from its purifying status occurs in two ways: The first: that one uses it for a devotional act (qurbah) — which (with a damm on the qaf) is an expression for doing an act for which reward is given, after knowing the One to whom one draws near, even if it does not depend on intention. As for obedience (ta'ah): it is an expression for doing an act for which reward is given, whether it depends on intention or not, whether one knows what he does for it or not. And worship ('ibadah): what gives reward for doing it, and depends on intention. Thus the five prayers, fasting, and similar are devotions, worships, and obediences. Reciting the Quran is a devotion and an obedience, not a worship. Contemplation leading to knowledge of Allah is an obedience, not a devotion nor worship. So it is in 'Hawashi al-Ashbah' by al-Hamawi. And what is meant by qurbah here is the reward itself, applying the name of the act to its result. So the conclusion: that which has been used for the purpose of acquiring reward is more general; whether impurity is removed by it, like ablution for removing impurity, or it is not removed, like ablution upon ablution, it is not permissible to purify with it. And the second: that one uses it for the purpose of removing impurity, whether it is also for a devotion, like intentional ablution, or like unintentional ablution according to us. By this it becomes clear to you that the relation between use for devotion and use for removal of impurity is that of general and specific from one perspective, and the word 'or' in the author's statement is for preventing emptiness, because combination is not impossible, and the 'lam' entering 'qurbah' is for purpose, but in the sense of consequence, not as something intended from the act and motivating it. Thus the objection that use for removal of impurity is inseparable from intention, so it does not include removal without intention, is repelled. And as for taking the 'lam' as indicating time, as chosen by the commentators, the commentator's estimation of that is in its place. And whoever wants further detail on the proofs should refer to extended works and not be deceived by the words of the glossator here, for the proofs of the Hanafis are apparent and clear in this matter, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling that water used for a devotional act (qurbah) or for removal of impurity (raf' hadath) loses its purifying property. The author first defines key terms: qurbah (devotion) is an act done for reward even without intention; ta'ah (obedience) is an act for reward whether with intention or not; 'ibadah (worship) is rewardable and requires intention. Examples: obligatory prayers are all three; Quran recitation is devotion and obedience but not worship; reflection on Allah is obedience only. The text then clarifies that 'used water' (ma' musta'mal) becomes invalid for purification in two cases: (1) when used for a devotional purpose (even without removing impurity, e.g., wudu on wudu), and (2) when used to remove impurity (even without devotional intention, e.g., unintentional wudu). The relationship between the two is general and specific from one perspective, meaning some actions fall under both, some under only one. The word 'or' (aw) in the original matn prevents the case where neither condition applies; the lam on 'qurbah' indicates purpose but in the sense of consequence, not necessarily the actor's conscious intention. This rebuts an objection that removal of impurity always involves intention, so unintentional removal would not be covered; but the lam is understood as consequence, not motive. The commentary ends by noting that Hanafi proofs on this are clear and refers to longer works.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act done for reward after knowing the one to whom one draws near, even if intention is not required.
طاعة (ta'ah): An act for which reward is given, whether or not it depends on intention.
عبادة ('ibadah): An act for which reward is given and requires intention.
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a devotional act or for removal of impurity, thereby losing its capacity to purify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, which of the following does NOT render water musta'mal?
A) Using water for a devotional prayer (qurbah) without removing impurity
B) Using water to remove impurity (raf' hadath) without devotional intent
C) Using water to wash a table after eating (no devotion or impurity removal)
D) Using water for a voluntary wudu (both devotion and impurity removal)

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal and loses purifying capacity if used for any devotional act or for removing impurity, regardless of intention.

The Definition and Causes of Musta'mal Water: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling and causes of water becoming musta'mal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of musta'mal water, identify the two causes according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Water becomes musta'mal by either removing hadath or performing qurbah – the majority Hanafi view.

Before diving into the dispute, we need a clear grasp of what makes water 'used' (musta'mal) and thus unsuitable for purification. The passage defines key terms like qurbah and hadath, then presents the majority and minority views within the Hanafi school. The outcome determines whether a person can reuse water that has already been in contact with a person in a state of ritual impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that using musta'mal water for wudu or ghusl is not permissible. Locate the statement 'ولا بماء استعمل لقربة أو لرفع حدث' and understand its implication.
This is the matn of al-Wiqayah, which the commentary expands upon.
2
Distinguish between qurbah, ta'ah, and ibadah
The commentator provides detailed definitions. Note the differences: qurbah is rewarded without intention, ta'ah is rewarded with or without intention, ibadah requires intention. Understand how reciting Quran is qurbah but not ibadah.
These definitions are from Hawashi al-Ashbah and are essential for the dispute.
3
State the two causes of musta'mal
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, water becomes musta'mal by either (1) removing hadath, even without intention, or (2) using it with the intention of qurbah. Confirm from the text: 'فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بإزالة الحدث، وأيضاً بنية القربة'.
Note the inclusive 'or' in the matn.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only intention of qurbah renders water musta'mal. Identify his reasoning: 'بأن الاستعمال إنما هو انتقال الآثام، وهو بالقربة'. Then see the commentator's dismissal: 'فليس بصحيح'.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, but the commentator favors the majority.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): if a person in hadath performs wudu without intention, the water becomes musta'mal according to the majority, but not according to Muhammad.
This affects whether that water can be reused for purification.

كتاب الطهارة/ أقسام المياه
ولا بماء استعمل لقربة أو لرفع حدث
اعلم أن في الماء المستعمل اختلافات : قوله : ولا بماء ؛ أي لا يجوز الوضوء بماء مستعمل، وكذا الغُسل واستعماله الذي يخرجه عن طهوريته، يكون بأمرين : أحدهما : أن يستعمله لأجل قُربة - وهي بالضم – : عبارة عن فعل ما يثاب عليه بعد معرفة من يتقرب إليه، وإن لم يتوقف على نية. وأما الطاعة : فهي عبارة عن فعل ما يثاب عليه توقف على نية أم لا، عرف ما يفعله لأجله أم لا. والعبادة : ما يثاب على فعله، ويتوقف على نيّة، فالصلوات الخمس والصوم ونحوها قُربات وعبادات وطاعات. وقراءة القرآن قُربة وطاعة لا عبادة. والنظر المؤدي إلى معرفة الله طاعة لا قربة ولا عبادة. كذا في «حواشي الأشباه» للحموي. والمراد بالقربة هاهنا نفس الثواب إطلاقاً لاسم الفعل على أثره، فالحاصل أنّ الذي استعمل لغرض تحصيل الثواب أعم من أن يرتفع به الحدث : كالوضوء لرفع الحدث، أو لم يرتفع : كالوضوء على الوضوء لا يجوز به التطهير. وثانيهما : أن يستعمله بغرض رفع حدث، سواء كان لقربة أيضاً : كالوضوء المنوي أو كالوضوء الغير المنوي عندنا. وبهذا وضح لك أنّ النسبة بين الاستعمال للقربة وبين الاستعمال لرفع الحدث، نسبة العموم والخصوص من وجه، وإن كلمة : «أو» في كلام المصنف لمنع الخلو؛ لعدم امتناع الجمع، وإن اللام الداخلة على القربة للغرض، لكن بمعنى العاقبة لا بما يكون مقصوداً من الفعل وباعثاً له، فاندفع ما أورد أنَّ الاستعمال لرفع الحدث لا ينفك عن النية، فلا يشمل رفعه بدون نيّة وأمّا حمل اللام على الوقت كما اختاره الناظرون الشارح له في تقدير ذلك في محله، ومن أراد الاستفاضة في أدلة ذلك فليراجع المطولات ولا يغتر بكلام المحشي هاهنا، فإن أدلة الحنفية ظاهرة جلية في هذا المقام، والله أعلم.
الأول : في أنه بأي شيء يصير مستعملاً ، فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بإزالة الحدث، وأيضاً بنية القربة، فإذا توضأ المحدث وضوء غيرَ منوي يصيرُ مستعملاً، ولو توضأ غير المحدثِ وضوء منوياً يصير مستعملاً أيضاً. وعند محمد بالثاني فقط فليس بصحيح
كما بسطناه في «السعاية»
قوله : بإزالة الحدث؛ أي النجاسة الغير الحقيقية، وأما المستعمل لإزالة النجاسات الحقيقية كماء الاستنجاء وغسالة الثياب النجسة فهو نجس اتفاقاً ما لم يعط للمغسول حكم الطهارة، وبعد ذلك هو طاهر وطهور اتفاقاً. كذا في «الغُنية» وغيرها، وما استعمل في غسل الأعيان الطاهرة طاهر بالاتفاق، كما في «التاتارخانية». قوله : وأيضاً؛ أي بكلِّ منهما اجتمعا أو تفرّقا؛ وذلك لأن الاستعمال بانتقال نجاسة الآثام إلى الماء، وأنها تزالُ بالقربة وإسقاط الفرض مؤثر أيضاً. كذا في «الهداية» و«البناية». وفي «فتح القدير»: «تتبع الروايات يفيد أن صيرورة الماء مستعملاً بأحد أمور ثلاثة : رفع الحدث تقرباً أو غير تقرب، والتقرب كان معه رفع حدث أو لم يكن، وسقوط الفرض عن العضو، وعليه تجري فروعُ إدخال اليد في الماء القليل لا الحاجة). قوله : بالثاني فقط؛ أي بنية القربة، بناءً على أنّ الاستعمال إنما هو انتقال الآثام، وهو بالقربة، وهذا هو المذكور في «الخلاصة» و«المحيط» وغيرهما.
Chapter of Purification / Categories of Water
And not with water used for a qurbah or for removing hadath.
Know that concerning used water there are differences. His statement: 'and not with water' means that it is not permissible to perform wudu with used water, likewise ghusl and its use which removes its purifying quality occurs through two matters: First: that he uses it for the sake of a qurbah – and it (qurbah) is, with dammah, an expression for doing that for which one is rewarded after knowledge of the One to whom one draws near, even if it does not depend on intention. As for ta‘ah, it is an expression for doing that for which one is rewarded, whether it depends on intention or not, whether one knows what one does for its sake or not. And ibadah is that for which one is rewarded and depends on intention. So the five prayers, fasting, and similar are qurbat, ibadat, and ta‘at. Recitation of Quran is qurbah and ta‘ah not ibadah. And contemplation leading to knowledge of Allah is ta‘ah not qurbah nor ibadah. Thus in Hawashi al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi. And the meaning of qurbah here is the reward itself, applying the name of the action to its effect. So the conclusion is that which is used for the purpose of attaining reward is general, whether hadath is removed by it like wudu for removing hadath, or not removed like wudu on top of wudu – purification is not permissible with it. Second: that he uses it for the purpose of removing hadath, whether it is also for qurbah like intentional wudu or like unintentional wudu according to us. And by this it is clear to you that the relationship between usage for qurbah and usage for removing hadath is generality and specificity from one aspect, and that the word 'or' in the author's speech is to prevent voidness because combination is not prohibited, and that the lam entering on qurbah is for purpose, but in the sense of consequence not as what is intended from the action and motivates it. Thus the objection that usage for removing hadath is not free from intention, so it does not include removal without intention, is repelled. As for carrying the lam on time as chosen by the observers, the commentator's estimation of that in its place is appropriate. And whoever wants extensive proofs on that should refer to lengthy works and not be deceived by the marginal annotator here, for the proofs of the Hanafis are clear and evident in this regard, and Allah knows best.
First: concerning by what thing it becomes used. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, by removing hadath, and also by intention of qurbah. So if a person in hadath performs wudu without intention, it becomes used. And if a person not in hadath performs wudu with intention, it also becomes used. According to Muhammad, by the second only, so it is not correct.
As we have elaborated in al-Si‘ayah.
His statement: 'by removing hadath' means the non-real impurity. As for water used for removing real impurities like water of istinja and washing of impure clothes, it is impure by agreement as long as the washed item has not been given the ruling of purity, and after that it is pure and purifying by agreement. Thus in al-Ghunyah and others. And what is used for washing pure objects is pure by agreement, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. His statement: 'and also' means by each of them whether combined or separate. That is because usage is by the transfer of the impurity of sins to water, and it is removed by qurbah and dropping the obligation is also effective. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Tracing the narrations indicates that water becomes used by one of three matters: removing hadath with qurbah or without qurbah, and qurbah whether with hadath or without, and the dropping of obligation from the limb. And upon this are based the branches of inserting the hand into a small quantity of water without need.' His statement: 'by the second only' means by intention of qurbah, based on the fact that usage is transfer of sins, and that is by qurbah. And this is what is mentioned in al-Khulasah, al-Muhit and others.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah, explaining the ruling that water used for a qurbah (act of worship) or for removing hadath (ritual impurity) becomes 'used water' (musta‘mal) and thus loses its purifying quality for further ritual use. The commentator first defines key terms: qurbah, ta‘ah, and ibadah. Qurbah is an act done to draw near to Allah, rewarded even without intention; ta‘ah is any rewarded act regardless of intention; ibadah requires intention. The passage then clarifies that the matn's 'or' is inclusive, meaning the water becomes used if either condition is met, or both. The central intra-Hanafi dispute is then introduced: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that water becomes used either by removing hadath or by performing an act with intention of qurbah. According to them, even an unintentional wudu by a person in hadath makes water used, and a deliberate wudu by a person not in hadath also makes it used. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, restricts the cause to qurbah (intention of drawing near) alone. The commentator notes that the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is more sound. The passage also distinguishes between used water (musta‘mal) and water that has removed physical impurity (najis), which is impure by consensus. The commentator references major Hanafi works like al-Hidayah, al-Binayah, and Fath al-Qadir to support the reasoning that the transfer of sins (athām) is the underlying cause, and this occurs through both qurbah and removal of hadath.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for either qurbah or removing hadath, losing its property of being purifying (tahur) for further ritual use.
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship performed to draw near to Allah, rewarded even without intention (e.g., reciting Quran).
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity (minor or major) that requires wudu or ghusl to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what are the two causes that make water musta'mal?
A) Only removing hadath
B) Only intention of qurbah
C) Either removing hadath or intention of qurbah
D) Removing physical impurity (najasah)

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal by either removing hadath or performing qurbah; the majority Hanafi view is relied upon for fatwa.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Causes and Timing of Water Becoming Musta'mal
Expounds the causes and timing of used water with intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on what causes water to become musta'mal and when it becomes musta'mal, and evaluate the cross-madhhab disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Water becomes used by either removing hadath or intending qurbah; timing is when it separates from the limb.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya delves into the definition and rulings of used water (musta'mal). The central question is: what transforms pure water into musta'mal (non-purifying for small quantities)? The Hanafi imams have differing views, and the Shafi'i school also weighs in. Additionally, there is a dispute on the precise moment it becomes used. This lesson unpacks these disagreements and establishes the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The first issue is: by what cause does water become musta'mal? The second is: at what moment does it become musta'mal?
The passage addresses both questions, but the primary focus is the causes.
2
State the Hanafi positions on causes
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that water becomes used by either removal of hadath (ritual impurity) or intention of qurbah (drawing near to Allah). Muhammad holds that only intention of qurbah suffices. The text declares Muhammad's view as 'not correct'.
The relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i position and Hanafi rebuttal
Al-Shafi'i maintains that only removal of hadath (which requires intention) makes water used. The Hanafi response uses the analogy of zakat vs. voluntary charity to show that both qurbah and isqat al-fard (dropping of obligation) are effective causes.
The rebuttal is from Fath al-Qadir.
4
Examine the timing dispute
After agreeing that water on the limb is not yet used, scholars differ: some say it becomes used upon separation from the limb, others after settling. The preferred view (al-Hidayah) is upon separation.
The reasoning: necessity suspends the ruling before separation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: water becomes musta'mal by either removal of hadath or intention of qurbah, and it becomes used as soon as it separates from the limb.
This is the view of the majority of later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول: في أنه بأي شيء يصير مستعملاً، فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف الله بإزالة الحدث، وأيضاً بنية القربة، فإذا توضأ المحدث وضوء غير منوي يصير مستعملاً، ولو توضأ غير المحدث وضوء منوياً يصير مستعملاً أيضاً. وعند محمد له بالثاني فقط فليس بصحيح (۱) كما بسطناه في «السعاية») [١] قوله: بإزالة الحدث؛ أي النجاسة الغير الحقيقية، وأما المستعمل لإزالة النجاسات الحقيقية كماء الاستنجاء وغسالة الثياب النجسة فهو نجس اتفاقاً ما لم يعط للمغسول حكم الطهارة، وبعد ذلك هو طاهر وطهور اتفاقاً. كذا في «الغنية» وغيرها، وما استعمل في غسل الأعيان الطاهرة طاهر بالاتفاق، كما في «التاتارخانية». [٢] قوله: وأيضاً؛ أي بكل منهما اجتمعا أو تفرقا؛ وذلك لأن الاستعمال بانتقال نجاسة الآثام إلى الماء، وأنها تزال بالقربة وإسقاط الفرض مؤثر أيضاً. كذا في «الهداية» و«البناية». وفي «فتح القدير»: «تتبع الروايات يفيد أن صيرورة الماء مستعملاً بأحد أمور ثلاثة: رفع الحدث تقرباً أو غير تقرب، والتقرب كان معه رفع حدث أو لم يكن، وسقوط الفرض عن العضو، وعليه تجري فروع إدخال اليد في الماء القليل لا الحاجة). [٣] قوله: بالثاني فقط؛ أي بنية القربة، بناءً على أن الاستعمال إنما هو انتقال الآثام، وهو بالقربة، وهذا هو المذكور في «الخلاصة» و«المحيط» وغيرهما. (۱) أي بنية القربة، واستدل أبو بكر الرازي لذلك بمسألة الجنب إذا انغمس في البئر لطلب الدلو، فقال محمد: الماء طاهر طهور؛ لعدم إقامة القربة، لكن قال السرخسي: تعليل محمد بعدم إقامة القربة ليس بقوي؛ لأنه غير مروي عنه، والصحيح عنه أن إزالة الحدث بالماء مفسدة له إلا عند الضرورة. ينظر: «البحر الرائق» (١: ٩٥-٩٦). (۲) «السعاية» (۱: ۳۹۲). (۳) «الهداية» (۱: ۸۹). (٤) انتهى من «فتح القدير»(۱: ۹۰). وعند الشافعي ه بإزالة الحدث لكن إزالة الحدث لا يتحقق إلا بنية القربة عنده بناءً على اشتراط النية في الوضوء. والاختلاف الثاني: في أنه متى يصير مستعملاً، ففي «الهداية»: إنه كما زايل العضو صار مستعملاً. وفي «البحر»: «هذا الخلاف إنما استنبطه أبو بكر الرازي له من مسألة الجنب إذا انغمس في البئر لطلب الدلو، فقال محمد له: إنه طاهر وطهور؛ لعدم إقامة القربة، وإن وجد معه رفع الحدث. وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي: التعليل بعدم إقامة القربة ليس بقوي؛ لأنه غير مروي عنه، والصحيح عنده أن إزالة الحدث بالماء أيضاً مفسدة إلا عند الضرورة: كالجنب يدخل البئر لطلب الدلو [١] قوله: وعند الشافعي له؛ وكذا عند زفر له مستنداً بأن مجرد القربة لا يدنس بل الإسقاط، ألا ترى أن المال لا يتدنّس بمجرد نية التقرّب، حتى يجوز دفع صدقة التطوع إلى الهاشمي، بخلاف الزكاة. وجوابه على ما في «فتح القدير» وغيره: «إن كلاً من التقرب المزيل للسيئات وإسقاط الفرض مؤثر، ألا ترى أنه انفرد وصف التقرّب في صدقة التطوع، حيث حرم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، والأثر عند ثبوت وصف الإسقاط أشد، حتى حرم الفرض على جميع بني هاشم، وبه خرج الجواب عن ما نسب إلى محمد الله له أيضا من كفاية (التقرب) [٢] قوله: والاختلاف الثاني؛ اعلم أنهم بعدما اتفقوا على أنه لا يعطى له حكم المستعمل ما دام على العضو اختلفوا في وقت كونه مستعملاً على قولين: أحدهما: أنه يصير مستعملاً بمزايلته عن البدن واستقراره في موضع، وهو اختيار مشايخ بلخ، والطحاوي، والظهير المرغيناني، والصدر الشهيد، وفخر الإسلام. (1) ينظر: «مغني المحتاج» (۱: ۲۰۰). (۲) انتهى من الهداية (۱: ۲۰)، وقال: لأن سقوط حكم الاستعمال قبل الانفصال للضرورة ولا ضرورة بعده. (۳) انتهى من «البحر الرائق»(٩٥-٩٦) بتصرف. (٤) انتهى من «فتح القدير» (۱: ۸۷).
The first: concerning by what thing it becomes used. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, by removal of hadath, and also by intention of qurbah. So if a person with hadath performs wudu without intention, it becomes used; and if a person without hadath performs wudu with intention, it also becomes used. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, it is only by the second [intention], and this is not valid. [1] as we expounded in al-Si'aya. [1] His saying: 'by removal of hadath' means non-real impurity. As for water used to remove real impurities, like istinja' water and washing of impure clothes, it is impure by consensus until it gives the washed item the ruling of purity; after that it is pure and purifying by consensus. Similarly in al-Ghunya and others. And water used for washing pure objects is pure by consensus, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. [2] His saying: 'also' means by each of them, whether combined or separate. This is because usage involves the transfer of sin impurity to water, and it is removed by qurbah, and the dropping of obligation is also effective. Similarly in al-Hidaya and al-Binaya. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Tracing the narrations indicates that water becomes used by one of three matters: removal of hadath with or without qurbah, qurbah whether accompanied by removal of hadath or not, and the dropping of the obligation from the limb; and upon this proceed the branches of inserting the hand into the small amount of water without need.' [3] His saying: 'only by the second' means by intention of qurbah, based on the fact that usage is the transfer of sins, and that is by qurbah. This is what is mentioned in al-Khulasa, al-Muhit, and others. (1) That is, by intention of qurbah, and Abu Bakr al-Razi argued for that with the case of a junub who immerses in a well to retrieve a bucket, so Muhammad said: the water is pure and purifying because qurbah was not established. But al-Sarakhsi said: Muhammad's reasoning by non-establishment of qurbah is not strong, because it is not narrated from him; the correct from him is that removal of hadath with water corrupts it except in necessity. See: al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (1:95-96). (2) al-Si'aya (1:392). (3) al-Hidaya (1:89). (4) End from Fath al-Qadir (1:90). And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, it is by removal of hadath, but removal of hadath is not realized except with intention of qurbah according to him, based on the condition of intention in wudu. The second disagreement: concerning when it becomes used. In al-Hidaya: 'when it separates from the limb it becomes used.' In al-Bahr: 'This disagreement was deduced by Abu Bakr al-Razi for him from the case of a junub who immerses in a well to retrieve a bucket, so Muhammad said to him: it is pure and purifying because qurbah was not established, even though removal of hadath occurred with it. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: the reasoning by non-establishment of qurbah is not strong, because it is not narrated from him; the correct according to him is that removal of hadath with water is also corrupting except in necessity, like the junub entering the well to retrieve the bucket. [1] His saying: 'and according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him', and similarly according to Zafar, may Allah have mercy on him, based on the fact that mere qurbah does not defile, but rather dropping (of obligation). Do you not see that wealth does not become defiled by mere intention of qurbah, so it is permissible to give voluntary charity to a Hashimi, contrary to zakat. And its answer according to Fath al-Qadir and others: 'Indeed, both the qurbah that removes sins and the dropping of obligation are effective. Do you not see that the description of qurbah alone is in voluntary charity, where it is prohibited for the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the effect when the description of dropping is established is stronger, so much so that the obligatory is prohibited to all Banu Hashim. And with this emerges the answer to what is attributed to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, also about the sufficiency of (qurbah). [2] His saying: 'the second disagreement': Know that after they agreed that it is not given the ruling of used water as long as it is on the limb, they disagreed about the time of its being used on two opinions: one: that it becomes used by its separation from the body and its settling in a place, and this is the choice of the scholars of Balkh, al-Tahawi, al-Zahir al-Marghinani, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and Fakhr al-Islam. (1) See: Mughni al-Muhtaj (1:200). (2) End from al-Hidaya (1:20), and he said: because the dropping of the ruling of usage before separation is due to necessity, and there is no necessity after it. (3) End from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (95-96) with modification. (4) End from Fath al-Qadir (1:87).
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion on the rulings of used water (musta'mal). It opens by stating the first issue: what causes water to become used? The author presents the positions of the major Hanafi imams. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, water becomes used in two ways: either by removing hadath (ritual impurity) or by performing a purificatory act with the intention of qurbah (drawing near to Allah). This applies even if the person has no hadath but intends qurbah, or has hadath but does not intend qurbah. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only intention of qurbah makes water used, not mere removal of hadath. The text notes that Muhammad's view is not considered correct (ليس بصحيح) — the relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The commentary then clarifies that water used to remove real impurities (like istinja' water) is impure by consensus before giving the washed item the ruling of purity, but after that it is pure and purifying. Water used on pure objects is pure by consensus. The reasoning behind the positions is that usage involves the transfer of 'impurity of sins' to the water, and this transfer occurs either by qurbah (which removes sins) or by dropping of the obligation (which also has an effect). This is supported by citations from al-Hidaya, al-Binaya, and Fath al-Qadir. The next part presents the Shafi'i view: water becomes used only by removal of hadath, but removal of hadath necessarily requires intention of qurbah in their school because they make intention a condition of wudu. The Hanafi response, quoted from Fath al-Qadir, argues that both qurbah and removal of obligation are effective; analogy with zakat and voluntary charity shows that mere qurbah is not sufficient to cause defilement of wealth, but when combined with obligation, the prohibition is stronger. This refutes the Shafi'i objection that intention alone cannot defile. The second issue is the timing of when water becomes used. There is agreement that water on the limb is not yet considered used. The dispute is whether it becomes used immediately upon separating from the limb or after settling. Al-Hidaya states it becomes used upon separation (the view of many later Hanafi scholars including the Balkh school, al-Tahawi, al-Zahir al-Marghinani, etc.). The reason is that before separation the ruling of usage is suspended due to necessity (the water is still needed for washing), but after separation there is no necessity. This is the preferred view.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification, i.e., water that has touched a limb in the context of wudu or ghusl and thus has acquired the ruling of being used (non-purifying when small amount).
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that prevents performance of prayer, etc., of two types: minor (hadath asghar) removed by wudu, and major (hadath akbar) removed by ghusl.
نية القربة (niyyat al-qurbah): The intention of drawing near to Allah by performing an act of worship (like wudu or ghusl) with the specific intent of obtaining reward or fulfilling a command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi position, when does water become musta'mal?
A) Only when it removes hadath with intention
B) Only when it is used with intention of qurbah
C) When it separates from the limb after use for either hadath removal or qurbah
D) Only after it has settled in a container

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal by either removal of hadath or intention of qurbah, and it becomes used as soon as it separates from the limb; this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Three Differences on Used Water
Explains three scholarly differences on definition, timing, and ruling of used water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on used water and explain why the relied-upon view is that it is pure but not purifying.

Core Idea
Used water removes sin but loses purifying power—a legal paradox resolved by analogy to charity's effect on Banu Hashim.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya uses an expansion probe to clarify three scholarly differences on used water. The first concerns what makes water 'used'; the second, when it becomes used; the third—most hotly contested—its legal ruling. Understanding these differences is essential for applying Hanafi purification rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three points of ikhtilaf
Locate where the author introduces the three differences (definition, timing, ruling). Note how each difference is framed as a distinct question.
The first difference is implicit: Shafi'i's view on definition is contrasted with the Hanafi approach.
2
Examine the second difference: timing
Two opinions: (1) used water only after separation from the body and settling; (2) used immediately upon separation. Identify which scholars held each view and which is preferred in al-Hidayah.
The necessity of the water staying on the limb during purification explains why it is not considered used until separation.
3
Analyze the third difference: ruling
Three Hanafi views: severe impurity (Abu Hanifa), light impurity (Abu Yusuf), pure but not purifying (Muhammad). Also note the Shafi'i/Maliki position that it remains purifying.
This is the core dispute; the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is based on different narrations and analogies.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the opposing school
The text provides an analogy to sadaqah: supererogatory charity purifies but is prohibited to the Prophet, while obligatory charity is prohibited to all Banu Hashim. Similarly, used water purifies the user but loses its purifying quality for further use.
The key point: the effect of obligation (isqat al-fard) is stronger than mere devotion, causing a legal 'defilement' of the water.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
Identify that Muhammad's view (pure but not purifying) is chosen by verifying scholars of Transoxiana, deemed the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and is the basis of fatwa.
This tarjih resolves the intra-Hanafi conflict for practical application.

According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) it is by removal of ritual impurity, but removal of ritual impurity is not achieved except with intention of devotion according to him based on stipulating intention in wudu. (2) The second difference: concerning when it becomes used (musta'mal). In al-Hidayah: Indeed, as soon as it leaves the limb it becomes used. In al-Bahr: This difference was deduced by Abu Bakr al-Razi from the issue of a junub who immerses in a well to retrieve a bucket. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said: It is pure and purifying due to lack of devotional intent, even though removal of ritual impurity occurs. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: The reasoning of lack of devotional intent is not strong because it is not reported from him; the correct view with him is that removal of ritual impurity with water is also corrupting except in necessity, like a junub entering a well to retrieve a bucket. [Footnote 1] His statement: According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and likewise according to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) based on the principle that mere devotion does not defile, but rather the removal (of impurity). Do you not see that wealth is not defiled by mere intention of devotion, such that it is permissible to give supererogatory charity to a Hashimi, unlike zakat? (r) And its response as in Fath al-Qadir and others: Indeed, both the devotion that removes sins and the fulfillment of an obligation are effective. Do you not see that the attribute of devotion alone applies to supererogatory charity, which was prohibited for the Prophet (peace be upon him), while the effect when the attribute of obligation exists is stronger, such that obligatory charity is prohibited for all Banu Hashim. And with this, the response is derived regarding what was attributed to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) about sufficiency of devotion ( ). [Footnote 2] His statement: The second difference: Know that after they agreed that it is not given the ruling of used water as long as it is on the limb, they differed on the time it becomes used in two opinions: One: It becomes used by its separation from the body and settling in a place. This is the choice of the scholars of Balkh, al-Tahawi, al-Zahir al-Marghinani, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and Fakhr al-Islam. (1) See: Mughni al-Muhtaj (1:200). (2) Ended from al-Hidayah (1:20), and he said: Because the removal of the ruling of being used before separation is due to necessity, and there is no necessity after it. (3) Ended from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (95-96) with modification. (4) Ended from Fath al-Qadir (1:87). [PAGE_388] 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya [1] The third difference: concerning its ruling: According to Abu Hanifa: It is impure with severe impurity. According to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him): It is impure with light impurity. According to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): It is pure but not purifying. (1). According to Malik and al-Shafi'i in his old opinion (3): It is pure and purifying. And the second (of the two opinions on the second difference): It becomes used by mere separation from the limb in wudu and from the entire body in ghusl, and this is what was chosen in al-Hidayah (3). [Footnote 1] His statement: 'concerning its ruling'; it would be better to say 'concerning its description'. [Footnote 2] His statement: 'According to ... etc.'; Know that three narrations are reported from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) concerning it (4): One: It is severely impure, reported by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (may Allah have mercy on him) and he adopted it; its basis is analogy on the property of sadaqah being purifying but prohibited for Banu Hashim, along with hadiths indicating the removal of sins by water. Second: It is mildly impure, reported by Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) and he adopted it; indeed, widespread occurrence affects the lightening of impurity. (1) See: Murshid Aqrab al-Masalik (p. 3), al-Murshid al-Mu'in, and its explanation Mukhtasar al-Durr al-Thamin al-Mawrid al-Mu'in (p. 23), Mukhtasar Khalil (p. 4), Hashiyat al-Dasuqi (1:42), al-Taj wa al-Iklil (1:66), and al-Fawakih al-Dawani (1:125), but they said: Used water in ritual purification is disliked. (2) Al-Shirbini said in Mughni al-Muhtaj (1:20) that the old Shafi'i school is that the water is purifying. (3) Al-Hidayah (1:90). (4) Al-Qari said in Fath Bab al-'Inaya (1:120): The scholars of Iraq did not confirm a difference among the three imams that used water is pure but not purifying, and the scholars of Transoxiana confirmed it. The difference in narration: From Abu Hanifa in the narration of al-Hasan from him, and it is his saying: It is impure with severe impurity. From Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa: It is impure with light impurity. From Muhammad, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa and it is more analogous: It is pure but not purifying. This narration was chosen by the verifying scholars of Transoxiana and others, and it is the apparent narration, and upon it is the fatwa.

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion probe commenting on the rulings of used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal) in the Hanafi school. The author presents three points of scholarly difference (ikhtilaf) related to used water, integrating intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes. The first difference concerns the definition: for Imam al-Shafi'i, used water is defined by its use in removing ritual impurity, which requires intention. The second difference concerns when water becomes classified as musta'mal. Two opinions are given: one that it becomes musta'mal only after separating from the body and settling elsewhere, preferred by many Hanafi scholars; the other that it becomes musta'mal immediately upon separation, which is the choice in al-Hidayah. The third difference is the most debated: the ruling itself. Three Hanafi positions are presented from Abu Hanifa (severe impurity), Abu Yusuf (light impurity), and Muhammad al-Shaybani (pure but not purifying). The Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold it to be pure and purifying. The text then explains the intra-Hanafi narration differences, noting that the position of Muhammad (pure but not purifying) is the most analogically sound (al-akyas) and the one relied upon for fatwa according to later scholars, especially those of Transoxiana. The proofs involve analogy (qiyas) with the property of sadaqah, which is purifying but prohibited to Banu Hashim, and hadiths about water removing sins. The passage guides students through the key disputes, emphasizing that the operative fatwa is the narration from Muhammad, which holds used water to be pure but not purifying.

Key Terms
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for ritual purification (wudu or ghusl) and has separated from the body.
النجاسة الغليظة (al-najasa al-ghaliza): Severe impurity that requires washing seven times, one with dust.
النجاسة المخففة (al-najasa al-mukhaffafa): Light impurity that requires washing once only.
إسقاط الفرض (isqat al-fard): The discharge/fulfillment of a religious obligation (fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling of water that has been used in wudu?
A) It is pure and purifying.
B) It is severely impure.
C) It is pure but not purifying.
D) It is mildly impure.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position on used water is that it is pure in essence but not purifying for further ritual use.

Taharah — Purification

The Third Difference: Ruling of Used Water in the Hanafi School
Expanding the third ikhtilāf on used water's ruling with intra-Hanafī transmissions and inter-madhhab comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on used water, explain the muftā bihī (ṭāhir ghayr ṭahūr), and compare it with the Shāfiʿī view using the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf).

Core Idea
Used water is pure but not purifying (ṭāhir ghayr ṭahūr) in the Hanafi muftā bihī, a unique category between impure and fully purifying.

Water used for wuḍūʾ or ghusl leaves the limb while carrying away sins—but what is its legal status afterward? This lesson unpacks the third major difference among Ḥanafī imāms and between madhāhib, revealing how qiyās, istiḥsān, and the subtlety of Abū Ḥanīfa’s reasoning shaped the ruling. You will learn why the relied-upon position (Muhammad al-Shaybānī’s) declares the water pure in itself but incapable of further purification, and how this affects daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
Locate the subject: water used for a valid wuḍūʾ or ghusl. Note that the ruling is about the water itself, not the act of purification.
The passage calls it al-māʾ al-mustaʿmal (used water).
2
Map the Hanafī ikhtilāf
List the three views from Abū Ḥanīfa (two transmissions via al-Ḥasan ibn Ziyād and Abū Yūsuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybānī. Identify the evidence each imam used.
Abū Ḥanīfa’s first view is najis ghalīẓ, second is najis khafīf; Muhammad’s is ṭāhir ghayr ṭahūr.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Compare the Ḥanafī muftā bihī with the Mālikī/Shāfiʿī positions. Note the practical difference: can one perform wuḍūʾ with this water again?
Shāfiʿī in old view says it is ṭāhir muṭahhir; new view says it becomes mustaʿmal upon leaving the limb.
4
Work through the qiyās argument
Examine the conditional proof: 'If it were pure, one could perform wuḍūʾ and then drink it in travel—but no one permits that.' Understand how this supports Abū Ḥanīfa’s view but is overridden by istiḥsān in the muftā bihī.
The fatwā follows Muhammad, which is the most moderate and strongest in evidence.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilāf
State the practical consequence: Ḥanafīs can use used water for non-purification (cooking, drinking) but not for wuḍūʾ or ghusl. Shāfiʿīs can reuse it for wuḍūʾ as long as it has not changed.
This distinction arises from the differing classification of the water.

(١) وعند مالك والشافعي في قوله القديم (۳) : هو طاهر مطهر. وثانيهما : إنّه يصير مستعملاً بمجرَّدِ زواله عن العضو في الوضوء، وعن جميع البدن في الغُسل، وهو الذي اختاره في «الهداية)(۳).
